# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

70-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer file that documents all the Java source files implementing Kafka's log compaction architecture. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've identified **13 key Java source files** in the apache/kafka repository that implement log compaction:

### Core Components:

1. **LogCleaner.java** - Main coordinator managing the pool of cleaner threads
2. **Cleaner.java** - Contains the actual deduplication and cleaning logic
3. **LogCleanerManager.java** - Implements segment selection policy
4. **OffsetMap.java & SkimpyOffsetMap.java** - Key-based deduplication using hash tables
5. Supporting files for configuration, statistics, transactions, and exceptions

### Key Mechanisms:

- **Cleaner Thread**: The `CleanerThread` inner class runs continuously, selecting the "filthiest" (dirtiest) log via `grabFilthiestCompactedLog()`
- **Segment Selection**: Logs are ranked by their `cleanableRatio` (cleanable bytes / total bytes)
- **Deduplication**: Uses `SkimpyOffsetMap` with MD5 hashing to build a key→latest_offset mapping, then filters out messages with older offsets

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains the complete list of files, key symbols, the execution call chain, and a detailed narrative explaining the architecture.

Kafka's support for very large stored log data makes it an excellent backend for an application built in this style.\n75: \n76: <h4 class=\"anchor-heading\"><a id=\"uses_commitlog\" class=\"anchor-link\"></a><a href=\"#uses_commitlog\">Commit Log</a></h4>\n77: \n78: Kafka can serve as a kind of external commit-log for a distributed system. The log helps replicate data between nodes and acts as a re-syncing\n79: mechanism for failed nodes to restore their data.\n80: The <a href=\"/documentation.html#compaction\">log compaction</a> feature in Kafka helps support this usage.\n81: In this usage Kafka is similar to <a href=\"https://bookkeeper.apache.org/\">Apache BookKeeper</a> project.\n82: ",

            "content": "660: \n661:     The log cleaner can be configured to retain a minimum amount of the uncompacted \"head\" of the log. This is enabled by setting the compaction time lag.\n662:     <pre class=\"language-text\"><code>log.cleaner.min.compaction.lag.ms</code></pre>\n663: \n664:     This can be used to prevent messages newer than a minimum message age from being subject to compaction. If not set, all log segments are eligible for compaction except for the last segment, i.e. the one currently\n665:     being written to. The active segment will not be compacted even if all of its messages are older than the minimum compaction time lag.\n666: \n667:     The log cleaner can be configured to ensure a maximum delay after which the uncompacted \"head\" of the log becomes eligible for log compaction.\n668:     <pre class=\"language-text\"><code>log.cleaner.max.compaction.lag.ms</code></pre>\n669: \n670: ...           {
            "content": "637: \n638:     <h4 class=\"anchor-heading\"><a id=\"design_compactiondetails\" class=\"anchor-link\"></a><a href=\"#design_compactiondetails\">Log Compaction Details</a></h4>\n639: \n640:     Log compaction is handled by the log cleaner, a pool of background threads that recopy log segment files, removing records whose key appears in the head of the log. Each compactor thread works as follows:\n641:     <ol>\n642:     <li>It chooses the log that has the highest ratio of log head to log tail\n643:     <li>It creates a succinct summary of the last offset for each key in the head of the log\n644:     <li>It recopies the log from beginning to end removing keys which have a later occurrence in the log. New, clean segments are swapped into the log immediately so the additional disk space required is just one\n645:     additional log segment (not a fully copy of the log).\n646: ... [chunk truncated]",
            "endLine": 648,

org.apache.kafka.common.TopicPartition;\\n20: import org.apache.kafka.common.config.AbstractConfig;\\n21: import org.apache.kafka.common.config.ConfigException;\\n22: import org.apache.kafka.common.errors.KafkaStorageException;\\n23: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.LogContext;\\n24: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Time;\\n25: import org.apache.kafka.config.BrokerReconfigurable;\\n26: import org.apache.kafka.server.config.ServerConfigs;\\n27: import org.apache.kafka.server.metrics.KafkaMetricsGroup;\\n28: import org.apache.kafka.server.util.ShutdownableThread;\\n29: import org.apache.kafka.storage.internals.utils.Throttler;\\n30: \\n31: import org.slf4j.Logger;\\n32: import org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;\\n33: \\n34: import java.io.File;\\n35: import java.io.IOException;\\n36: import java.security.DigestException;\\n37: import java.security.NoSuchAlgorithmException;\\n38: import java.util.ArrayList;\\n39: import java.util.List;\\n40: import java.util.Map;\\n41: import java.util.Optional;\\n42: import java.util.Set;\\n43: import java.util.concurrent.ConcurrentMap;\\n44: import java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\\n45: import java.util.function.Function;\\n46: import java.util.stream.Collectors;\\n47: import java.util.stream.IntStream;\\n48: \\n49: /**\\n50:  * The cleaner is responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \\\"compact\\\" retention strategy.\\n51:  * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\\n52:  * <p>\\n53:  * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \\\"clean\\\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\\n54:  * \\\"dirty\\\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \\\"cleanable\\\" section followed by an \\\"uncleanable\\\" section.\\n55:  * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\\n56:  * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\\n57:  * <p>\\n58:  * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \\\"compact\\\" retention policy\\n59:  * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\\n60:  * <p>\\n61:  * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\\n62:  * the implementation of the mapping.\\n63:  * <p>\\n64:  * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\\n65:  * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\\n66:  * <p>\\n67:  * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\\n68:  * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\\n69:  * <p>\\n70:  * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\\n71:  * <p>\\n72:  * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\\n73:  * <p>\\n74:  * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\\n75:  * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\\n76:  * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\\n77:  * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\\n78:  * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\\n79:  * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\\n80:  * <p>\\n81:  * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\\n82:  * are the key points:\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  * <ol>\\n85:  * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\\n86:  *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\\n87:  *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\\n88:  * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\\n89:  *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\\n90:  *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\\n91:  * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\\n92:  * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\\n93:  *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\\n94:  *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\\n95:  *    tombstone deletion.</li>\\n96:  * </ol>\\n97:  */\\n98: public class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\\n99:     private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(LogCleaner.class);\\n100: \\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaner.java%3FL1-100\"}",

java.util.stream.Collectors;\n47: import java.util.stream.IntStream;\n48: \n49: /**\n50:  * The cleaner is responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \"compact\" retention strategy.\n51:  * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\n52:  * <p>\n53:  * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \"clean\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\n54:  * \"dirty\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \"cleanable\" section followed by an \"uncleanable\" section.\n55:  * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\n56:  * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\n57:  * <p>\n58:  * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \"compact\" retention policy\n59:  * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\n60:  * <p>\n61:  * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\n62:  * the implementation of the mapping.\n63:  * <p>\n64:  * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\n65:  * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\n66:  * <p>\n67:  * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\n68:  * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\n69:  * <p>\n70:  * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\n71:  * <p>\n72:  * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\n73:  * <p>\n74:  * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\n75:  * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\n76:  * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\n77:  * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\n78:  * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\n79:  * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\n80:  * <p>\n81:  * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\n82:  * are the key points:\n83:  * <p>\n84:  * <ol>\n85:  * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\n86:  *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. log compaction feature is implemented across multiple Java source files in the `storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/` directory. The architecture consists of three main components:\\n\\n### 1. The Cleaner Thread Implementation\\n\\nThe **LogCleaner.java** file serves as the main coordinator for log compaction. It implements `BrokerReconfigurable` and manages a pool of background cleaner threads. The key inner class is **CleanerThread**, which extends `ShutdownableThread` and implements the thread that performs the actual cleaning work.\\n\\nThe cleaning lifecycle in LogCleaner.cleanFilthiestLog() follows this sequence:\\n1. Uses LogCleanerManager.grabFilthiestCompactedLog() to select the log with the highest ratio of dirty bytes to total bytes\\n2. Builds an offset map for the dirty section using Cleaner.buildOffsetMap()\\n3. Cleans the segments using Cleaner.cleanSegments()\\n4. Replaces the old segments with cleaned ones\\n\\n### 2. Segment Selection Policy\\n\\nThe **LogCleanerManager.java** file implements the segment selection policy. Key methods include:\\n\\n- **grabFilthiestCompactedLog()** - Selects the log with the highest cleanable ratio (dirtiest log), implementing the policy of choosing logs that benefit most from cleaning\\n- **calculateCleanableBytes()** - Computes the number of cleanable bytes between the first dirty offset and the first uncleanable offset\\n\\nThe **LogToClean.java** class represents a log selected for cleaning and compares logs by their `cleanableRatio`, which is calculated as `cleanableBytes / totalBytes`. This ratio determines which log is \\\"filthiest\\\" and should be cleaned next.\\n\\n### 3. Key-Based Deduplication Logic\\n\\nThe deduplication logic uses two key classes:\\n\\n- **OffsetMap.java** (interface) - Defines the contract for the deduplication map with methods: put(), get(), updateLatestOffset(), clear(), size(), slots(), and latestOffset()\\n\\n- **SkimpyOffsetMap.java** (implementation) - Implements the actual deduplication map using a cryptographically secure hash (MD5 by default) to map keys to their latest offsets. It uses:\\n  - Hash table with collision resolution via probing\\n  - MessageDigest for hashing keys to save memory overhead\\n  - No delete support (only put and get operations)\\n  - Configurable hash algorithms (MD2, MD5, SHA-1, SHA-256, SHA-384, SHA-512)\\n\\nThe **Cleaner.java** class contains the core deduplication logic:\\n\\n- **buildOffsetMap()** - Builds the key=>offset mapping for the dirty section of the log by reading messages and storing the latest offset for each key\\n- **buildOffsetMapForSegment()** - Processes individual segments to populate the offset map\\n- **cleanSegments()** - Uses the offset map to deduplicate: for each message in a segment, it checks if a newer message with the same key exists in the offset map (in the head/dirty portion). If so, the message is discarded; otherwise, it's retained in the cleaned segment\\n\\n### Supporting Components\\n\\n- **CleanerConfig.java** - Provides configuration parameters for the cleaner (buffer size, thread count, I/O rates, etc.)\\n- **CleanerStats.java** - Collects cleaning statistics (bytes read/written, messages processed, timing info)\\n- **PreCleanStats.java** - Collects pre-cleaning statistics (max compaction delays, cleanable partitions count)\\n- **CleanedTransactionMetadata.java** - Handles transaction state during cleaning, manages aborted transactions and control markers\\n- **LogCleaningException.java** and **LogCleaningAbortedException.java** - Handle cleaning-related errors\\n- **LogCleaningState.java** - Tracks the state of each partition being cleaned (None, InProgress, Aborted, Paused)\\n\\nThe architecture efficiently implements log compaction by separating concerns: the LogCleanerManager handles selection policy, Cleaner handles the actual deduplication using the OffsetMap for efficient key lookup, and CleanerThread manages the execution lifecycle.\"\n}\n",
